     <p>
      <i>
       <b>
        A Night at the Opera
       </b>
      </i>
      is the fourth studio album by the British rock band
      <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">
       Queen
      </a>
      , released in November 1975. Co-produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Roy_Thomas_Baker" title="Roy Thomas Baker">
       Roy Thomas Baker
      </a>
      and Queen, it was the most expensive album ever recorded at the time of its release.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicqueen_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-allmusicqueen-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A commercial success,
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      has been voted by the public and cited by music publications as one of Queen's finest works.
     </p>
     <p>
      The album takes its name from the
      <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers#Filmography" title="Marx Brothers">
       Marx Brothers film
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(film)" title="A Night at the Opera (film)">
        A Night at the Opera
       </a>
      </i>
      , which the band watched one night at the studio complex when recording.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-storydoc_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-storydoc-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was originally released by
      <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">
       EMI
      </a>
      in the United Kingdom, where it topped the
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">
       UK Albums Chart
      </a>
      for four non-consecutive weeks, and
      <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">
       Elektra Records
      </a>
      in the United States, where it peaked at No. 4 on the
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       200
      </a>
      and became the band's first platinum selling album in the US.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

         <span class="tocnumber">
          8
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          External links
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Song_information">
       Song information
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Song information">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Death_On_Two_Legs_.28Dedicated_to.....29.22">
       "Death On Two Legs (Dedicated to....)"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title='Edit section: "Death On Two Legs (Dedicated to....)"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs_(Dedicated_to...)" title="Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)">
       Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs_(Dedicated_to...)" title="Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)">
       Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)
      </a>
      " could only be referred to as
      <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">
       Freddie Mercury
      </a>
      's hate letter towards Queen's ex-manager,
      <a href="/wiki/Norman_Sheffield" title="Norman Sheffield">
       Norman Sheffield
      </a>
      , who for some years was reputed to have mistreated the band and abused his role as their manager from 1972 to 1975; however this was later denied in an autobiography by Sheffield published in 2013 titled "Life on Two Legs: Set The Record Straight"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      where Sheffield denies such rumours and refers to copies of the original 1972 Queen management contracts between Sheffield and Queen included in the book as proof to back up his defence. Though the song never made a direct reference to him, upon listening to a playback of the song at
      <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">
       Trident Studios
      </a>
      during the time of album release, Sheffield was appalled and sued the band and the record label for defamation which resulted in an out of court settlement,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and this later revealed to the public his connection to the song.
     </p>
     <p>
      During live performances, Mercury would usually rededicate the song to "a real
      <a href="/wiki/Motherfucker" title="Motherfucker">
       motherfucker
      </a>
      of a gentleman", although this line was censored on the version that appeared on their
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Live_Killers" title="Live Killers">
        Live Killers
       </a>
      </i>
      album in 1979. Other than on the version of said live album, he'd said it was dedicated to a "motherfucker I used to know".
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Classic_Albums" title="Classic Albums">
        Classic Albums
       </a>
      </i>
      documentary about the making of
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">
       Brian May
      </a>
      stated that the band at first was somewhat taken aback by the incisiveness of Mercury's lyrics and described by Mercury as being, "so vindictive that Brian felt bad singing it.".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicalbums_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-classicalbums-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the song came together, it was agreed that the "author should have his way", and the song went on as penned.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicalbums_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-classicalbums-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As with "
      <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">
       Bohemian Rhapsody
      </a>
      ", most of the guitar parts on this song were initially played on piano by Mercury, to demonstrate to May how they needed to be played on guitar. "Death on Two Legs" remained on the setlist until, and well into,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Tour" title="The Game Tour">
       The Game Tour
      </a>
      in 1980, then was dropped. The piano introduction though was played through the
      <i>
       Hot Space
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Works
      </i>
      tours.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Lazing_on_a_Sunday_Afternoon.22">
       "Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title='Edit section: "Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      "Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon" is another song by Mercury. He played piano and did all of the vocals. The lead vocal was sung in the studio and reproduced through headphones in a tin bucket elsewhere in the studio. A microphone picked up the sound from the bucket, which gives it a hollow "megaphone" sound. The guitar solo is also reported to have been recorded on the vocal track, as there were no more tracks to record on, as explained by producer Roy Thomas Baker during the 'Classic Albums' documentary. The key change going into the guitar solo (Eb to A) is a tritone relationship, making it a jarring, but very effective, transition into the key of E minor for the next track, "I'm in Love with My Car".
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22I.27m_in_Love_with_My_Car.22">
       "I'm in Love with My Car"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: &quot;I'm in Love with My Car&quot;">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/I%27m_in_Love_with_My_Car" title="I'm in Love with My Car">
       I'm in Love with My Car
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/I%27m_in_Love_with_My_Car" title="I'm in Love with My Car">
       I'm in Love with My Car
      </a>
      " is amongst
      <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">
       Roger Taylor
      </a>
      's most famous songs in the Queen catalogue. The song was initially taken as a joke by May, who thought that Taylor was not serious when he heard a demo recording.
     </p>
     <p>
      Taylor played the guitars in the original demo, but they were later re-recorded by May on his
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">
       Red Special
      </a>
      . The lead vocals were performed by Taylor on the studio version, and all released live versions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The revving sounds at the conclusion of the song were recorded by Taylor's then current car, an
      <a href="/wiki/Alfa_Romeo" title="Alfa Romeo">
       Alfa Romeo
      </a>
      . The lyrics were inspired by one of the band's
      <a href="/wiki/Road_crew" title="Road crew">
       roadies
      </a>
      , Johnathan Harris, whose
      <a href="/wiki/Triumph_TR4" title="Triumph TR4">
       Triumph TR4
      </a>
      was evidently the "love of his life". The song is dedicated to him, the album says: "Dedicated to Johnathan Harris, boy racer to the end".
     </p>
     <p>
      When it came down to releasing the album's first single, Taylor was so fond of his song that he urged Mercury (author of the first single, "Bohemian Rhapsody") to allow it to be the B-side and reportedly locked himself in a cupboard until Mercury agreed. This decision would later become the cause of much internal friction in the band, in that while it was only the B-side, it generated an equal amount of publishing royalties for Taylor as the main single did for Mercury.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The song was often played live during the 197781 period. Taylor sang it from the drums while Mercury played piano and provided backing vocals. It was played in the
      <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers_Tour" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour">
       Queen + Paul Rodgers Tour
      </a>
      in 2005 and the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_the_Cosmos_Tour" title="Rock the Cosmos Tour">
       Rock the Cosmos Tour
      </a>
      in 2008. Taylor would again play the song for his concerts with
      <a href="/wiki/The_Cross_(band)" title="The Cross (band)">
       The Cross
      </a>
      and solo tours, where instead of drums he played rhythm guitar.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22You.27re_My_Best_Friend.22">
       "You're My Best Friend"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: &quot;You're My Best Friend&quot;">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/You%27re_My_Best_Friend_(Queen_song)" title="You're My Best Friend (Queen song)">
       You're My Best Friend (Queen song)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "You're My Best Friend" was Queen's first single written by
      <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">
       John Deacon
      </a>
      . He composed while he was learning to play piano. He played the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wurlitzer_Electric_Piano" title="Wurlitzer Electric Piano">
       Wurlitzer Electric Piano
      </a>
      (which Mercury called a "horrible" instrument in an interview) on the recording and overdubbed the bass later on. The song was written for his wife, Veronica Tetzlaff. The song was a top 10 hit.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22.2739.22">
       "'39"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: &quot;'39&quot;">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/%2739_(Queen_song)" title="'39 (Queen song)">
       '39 (Queen song)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "'39" was May's attempt to do "
      <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">
       sci-fi
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">
       skiffle
      </a>
      ". "'39" relates the tale of a group of space explorers who embark on what is, from their perspective, a year-long voyage. Upon their return, however, they realise that a hundred years have passed, because of the
      <a href="/wiki/Time_dilation" title="Time dilation">
       time dilation
      </a>
      effect in
      <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">
       Einstein
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
       special theory of relativity
      </a>
      , and the loved ones they left behind are now all dead or aged.
     </p>
     <p>
      May sings the song on the album, with backing vocals by Mercury and Taylor. During live performances, Mercury sang the lead vocal.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      May had asked bassist
      <a href="/wiki/John_Deacon" title="John Deacon">
       John Deacon
      </a>
      to play
      <a href="/wiki/Double_bass" title="Double bass">
       double bass
      </a>
      as a joke but a couple of days later he found Deacon in the studio with the instrument, and he had already learned to play it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_Legends_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Queen_Legends-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Since Queen had named their albums
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Day_at_the_Races_(album)" title="A Day at the Races (album)">
        A Day at the Races
       </a>
      </i>
      after two of the
      <a href="/wiki/Marx_Brothers" title="Marx Brothers">
       Marx Brothers
      </a>
      ' most popular films, surviving brother
      <a href="/wiki/Groucho_Marx" title="Groucho Marx">
       Groucho Marx
      </a>
      invited Queen to visit him at his Los Angeles home in March 1977 (five months before he died). The band thanked him, and performed "'39" a cappella.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">
       George Michael
      </a>
      performed "'39" at the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">
       Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert
      </a>
      in April 1992.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Michael cited this song as his favourite Queen song, claiming he used to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Busking" title="Busking">
       busk
      </a>
      it on the
      <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">
       London Underground
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Recently, Queen have included the song on the setlists of their
      <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Adam_Lambert" title="Queen + Adam Lambert">
       tours
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lambert" title="Adam Lambert">
       Adam Lambert
      </a>
      ; as on the album, it is sung by May.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Sweet_Lady.22">
       "Sweet Lady"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title='Edit section: "Sweet Lady"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      "Sweet Lady" is a distortion-driven fast rocker written by May. The song is an unusual rock style in 3/4 meter (which gives way to 4/4 at the bridge). Taylor remembers it as the most difficult drumming part he ever recorded.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Attribution_needed" title="Wikipedia:Attribution needed">
         <span title="This sentence may contain perspectives and opinions without stating whose they are. (November 2011)">
          attribution needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The backing track was probably recorded live as you can hear the snare wires on the snare drum of Taylor's kit vibrating along with Deacon's bass guitar riff.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Seaside_Rendezvous.22">
       "Seaside Rendezvous"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title='Edit section: "Seaside Rendezvous"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      "Seaside Rendezvous", written by Mercury, is notable for the mock-instrumental bridge section which begins at around 0:51 into the song. The section is performed entirely by Mercury and Taylor using their voices alone. Mercury imitates woodwind instruments including a
      <a href="/wiki/Clarinet" title="Clarinet">
       clarinet
      </a>
      and Taylor mostly brass instruments, including
      <a href="/wiki/Tuba" title="Tuba">
       tubas
      </a>
      and trumpets, and even a
      <a href="/wiki/Kazoo" title="Kazoo">
       kazoo
      </a>
      ; during this section Taylor hits the highest note on the album,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soprano_C" title="Soprano C">
       C6
      </a>
      . The "tap dance" segment is performed by Mercury and Taylor on the mixing desk with
      <a href="/wiki/Thimble" title="Thimble">
       thimbles
      </a>
      on their fingers. Mercury plays both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_piano" title="Grand piano">
       grand piano
      </a>
      and jangle honky-tonk.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22The_Prophet.27s_Song.22">
       "The Prophet's Song"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: &quot;The Prophet's Song&quot;">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/The_Prophet%27s_Song" title="The Prophet's Song">
       The Prophet's Song
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Prophet's Song was composed by May (working title "People of the Earth"). On the show
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_the_Studio_with_Redbeard" title="In the Studio with Redbeard">
        In the Studio with Redbeard
       </a>
      </i>
      , which spotlighted
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      , May explained that he wrote the song after a dream he'd had about a great flood while he was recovering from being ill while recording the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sheer_Heart_Attack" title="Sheer Heart Attack">
        Sheer Heart Attack
       </a>
      </i>
      album, and is the source of some of the lyrics. He spent several days putting it together, and it includes a vocal
      <a href="/wiki/Canon_(music)" title="Canon (music)">
       canon
      </a>
      sung by Mercury. The vocal, and later instrumental canon was produced by early
      <a href="/wiki/Delay_(audio_effect)" title="Delay (audio effect)">
       tape delay
      </a>
      devices. It is a heavy and dark number with a strong
      <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">
       progressive rock
      </a>
      influence and challenging lead vocals. At over eight minutes in length, it's also Queen's longest song (not counting the
      <a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven#.5BUntitled_Hidden_Track.5D" title="Made in Heaven">
       untitled instrumental track
      </a>
      on "
      <a href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven" title="Made in Heaven">
       Made in Heaven
      </a>
      ").
     </p>
     <p>
      As detailed by May in a documentary about the album, the speed-up effect that happens in the middle of the guitar solo was achieved by starting a reel-to-reel player with the tape on it, as the original tape player was stopped.
     </p>
     <p>
      The dream May had was about
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_Flood" title="The Great Flood">
       The Great Flood
      </a>
      , and lyrics have references from the Bible and the
      <a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark" title="Noah's Ark">
       Noah's Ark
      </a>
      account.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Love_of_My_Life.22">
       "Love of My Life"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title='Edit section: "Love of My Life"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">
       Love of My Life (Queen song)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "Love of My Life" was written for Mercury's girlfriend at the time, Mary Austin, and is one of his most covered songs (there have been versions by many acts like
      <a href="/wiki/Extreme_(band)" title="Extreme (band)">
       Extreme
      </a>
      featuring May,
      <a href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)" title="Scorpions (band)">
       Scorpions
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Elaine_Paige" title="Elaine Paige">
       Elaine Paige
      </a>
      ). Mercury played piano (including a classical solo) and did all of the vocals with startling
      <a href="/wiki/Multitrack_recording" title="Multitrack recording">
       multi-tracking
      </a>
      precision. May played
      <a href="/wiki/Harp" title="Harp">
       harp
      </a>
      (doing it chord by chord and pasting the takes to form the entire part),
      <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Hummingbird" title="Gibson Hummingbird">
       Gibson Hummingbird
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">
       acoustic guitar
      </a>
      (which he'd bought in Japan) and his Red Special.
     </p>
     <p>
      Brian May eventually arranged the song so it could be played on an acoustic 12 string for live performances.
     </p>
     <p>
      "Love of My Life" was such a concert favourite that Mercury frequently stopped singing and allowed the audience to take over. It was especially well received during concerts in South America, and the band released the song as a single there. When Queen and
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers" title="Paul Rodgers">
       Paul Rodgers
      </a>
      performed the song (specifically Brian solo) he sang almost none of the words and let the audience sing it all, continuing the tradition.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Good_Company.22">
       "Good Company"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title='Edit section: "Good Company"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Company_(song)" title="Good Company (song)">
       Good Company (song)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "Good Company" was written and sung by May, who provides all vocals and plays a "Genuine Aloha" ukulele.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The recording is remarkable for featuring an elaborate recreation of a
      <a href="/wiki/Dixieland" title="Dixieland">
       Dixieland
      </a>
      -style jazz band, produced by way of May's
      <a href="/wiki/Red_Special" title="Red Special">
       Red Special
      </a>
      guitar and Deacy Amp. Brian May composed the song on a
      <a href="/wiki/Banjo_uke" title="Banjo uke">
       Banjo ukelele
      </a>
      , but recorded the song with a regular ukulele instead.
     </p>
     <p>
      The song is a
      <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">
       narrative
      </a>
      tale, told by a man who in young age was advised by his father to "take care of those you call your own, and keep good company". In his younger years, the singer follows his father's advice, keeping his friends and marrying a girl named Sally. However, after their marriage, he begins to lose interest in his friends, who gradually disappear. As he grows older, he becomes increasingly skilled at and dedicated to his occupation, working long nights and neglecting his family.
     </p>
     <p>
      Eventually, the man's efforts are rewarded, he begins his own
      <a href="/wiki/Limited_company" title="Limited company">
       Limited company
      </a>
      (which is also a pun, since throughout the rest of the song "company" is used in the sense of companions). Ever more dedicated to his business, he hardly notices as his wife leaves him.
     </p>
     <p>
      The song finishes with the speaker as an elderly man, puffing on his pipe and pondering the lessons of his life, which he has no one left to share with.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22Bohemian_Rhapsody.22">
       "Bohemian Rhapsody"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title='Edit section: "Bohemian Rhapsody"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">
       Bohemian Rhapsody
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      "Bohemian Rhapsody" was written by Mercury with the first guitar solo composed by May. All piano, bass and drum parts, as well as the vocal arrangements, were thought up by Mercury on a daily basis and written down "in blocks" (using note names instead of sheets) on a phonebook. The other members recorded their respective instruments with no concept of how their tracks would be utilised in the final mix. The now famous operatic section was originally intended to be only a short interlude of "Galileos" that connected the ballad and hard rock portions of the song.
     </p>
     <p>
      During the recording, the song became affectionately known as "Fred's Thing" to the band, and the title only emerged during the final sessions.
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite being twice as long as the average single in 1975 and garnering mixed critical reviews initially, the song became immensely popular, topping charts worldwide (where it remained for an unprecedented nine weeks in the UK) and is now widely regarded as one of the most significant rock songs in history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nyt-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After Freddie Mercury's death, the song was rereleased as a double A-side to "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/These_Are_The_Days_Of_Our_Lives" title="These Are The Days Of Our Lives">
       These Are The Days Of Our Lives
      </a>
      " on 9 December 1991 in the UK and September 5, 1991 in US.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".22God_Save_the_Queen.22">
       "God Save the Queen"
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title='Edit section: "God Save the Queen"'>
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      May recorded a cover version of
      <a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">
       God Save the Queen
      </a>
      , the British national anthem, in 1974 before their
      <i>
       Sheer Heart Attack
      </i>
      tour. He played a guide piano which was edited out later and added several layers of guitars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicalbums_8-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-classicalbums-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the song was completed it was played as an outro at virtually every concert while the band were taking their bows. When recording the track May played a rough version on piano for Roy Thomas Baker. He called his own skills on the piano sub-par at the time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-classicalbums_8-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-classicalbums-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He performed the song live on the roof of
      <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">
       Buckingham Palace
      </a>
      for the Queen's
      <a href="/wiki/Golden_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Golden Jubilee of Elizabeth II">
       golden jubilee
      </a>
      in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      May has stated that he performed the song on the roof of Buckingham Palace as a
      <a href="/wiki/Homage_(arts)" title="Homage (arts)">
       homage
      </a>
      to
      <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">
       Jimi Hendrix
      </a>
      's version of "
      <a href="/wiki/The_Star-Spangled_Banner" title="The Star-Spangled Banner">
       The Star-Spangled Banner
      </a>
      ".
     </p>
     <p>
      Guitar layering is one of May's distinctive techniques as a rock guitarist. He has said that the technique was developed whilst looking for a violin sound. For tracks like this, he stated he can use "up to 30" layers, using a small amplifier named the '
      <a href="/wiki/Deacy_Amp" title="Deacy Amp">
       Deacy Amp
      </a>
      ' built by Deacon, and later released commercially like the "Brian May" amplifier by Vox.
     </p>
     <p>
      "God Save the Queen" is the only-ever song recorded by Queen that was not written by any of the band members, but May is credited as its arranger.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception_and_legacy">
       Reception and legacy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">

        ]

      </span>

         <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
         <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
         <img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
        </span>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uncut_25-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-uncut-25">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          25
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      At the time the most expensive album ever recorded,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusicqueen_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-allmusicqueen-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      May has asserted in subsequent years that, had
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      not been successful, Queen would have disbanded.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Upon release, the album was a commercial success, debuting at No. 1 in the UK and topping the charts for four non-consecutive weeks. In the US, it reached No. 4, the band's strongest showing at that time.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      In
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1977_Grammy_Awards" title="1977 Grammy Awards">
       1977
      </a>
      "
      <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">
       Bohemian Rhapsody
      </a>
      " received two
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">
       Grammy Award
      </a>
      nominations for
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocals#1970s" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocals">
       Best Pop Vocal Performance by a Duo, Group or Chorus
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Vocal_Arrangement_for_Two_or_More_Voices#1970s" title="Grammy Award for Best Vocal Arrangement for Two or More Voices">
       Best Arrangement for Voices
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a contemporary review, Kris Nicholson of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine said that, although they share other heavy metal groups' penchant for "manipulating dynamics," Queen are an elite act in the genre and set themselves apart by incorporating "unlikely effects: acoustic piano, harp, acapella vocals, no synthesisers. Coupled with good songs."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rstone_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-rstone-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">
        Melody Maker
       </a>
      </i>
      called the album a "must-have", encouraging listeners to "turn it up loud and enjoy",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melodymaker_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-melodymaker-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Free_Press" title="Winnipeg Free Press">
        Winnipeg Free Press
       </a>
      </i>
      wrote: "The group's potential is practically limitless, indicating that Queen is destined to finally take its place among the small handful of truly major acts working in rock today."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-winnipeg_29-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-winnipeg-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">
       Robert Christgau
      </a>
      , writing in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">
        The Village Voice
       </a>
      </i>
      , felt that the album "doesn't actually botch any of a half-dozen arty-to-heavy 'eclectic' modes ... and achieves a parodic tone often enough to suggest more than meets the ear." However, he questioned what "that more is".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christgau_20-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-christgau-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In a retrospective review for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">
       Allmusic
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">
       Stephen Thomas Erlewine
      </a>
      called the album "a self-consciously ridiculous and overblown hard rock masterpiece" and "
      <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">
       prog rock
      </a>
      with a sense of humour as well as dynamics". Erlewine felt that Queen "never bettered their approach anywhere else".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic2_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-allmusic2-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2006 review,
      <i>
       Q
      </i>
      also felt that they never topped the album, which the magazine said "remains glorious, monumental" as British rock music's "greatest extravagance."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Q2006_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Q2006-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">
        Uncut
       </a>
      </i>
      noted "the extent of the band's barmy diversity."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uncut_25-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-uncut-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Mojo
      </i>
      called the album "an imperial extravaganza, a cornucopia", and Queen "a band of hungrily competitive individualists on a big roll of friendship and delight."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mojo-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">
       Pitchfork Media
      </a>
      's Dominique Leone said that the band topped their contemporaries on the album without limiting themselves or sparing any effort.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pitchfork-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/Rhapsody_(online_music_service)" title="Rhapsody (online music service)">
       Rhapsody
      </a>
      's Mike McGuirk,
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      is often viewed as one of the greatest rock albums of all time. McGuirk felt that the album's combination of heavy metal, recording effects, theatrical sophistication, and British grandeur still make for an engaging listen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rhapsody_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-rhapsody-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
       BBC
      </a>
      said of the record: "Christmas 1975 was to be forever remembered as Queens. And
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      remains their finest hour."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbc-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Re-releases">
       Re-releases
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Re-releases">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The album was first re-released in the US on Hollywood Records on 3 September 1991 with two bonus remixes, as part of a complete re-release of all Queen albums.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 30 April 2002 the album was again re-released on
      <a href="/wiki/DVD-Audio" title="DVD-Audio">
       DVD-Audio
      </a>
      with a 5.1-channel mix in
      <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Digital" title="Dolby Digital">
       Dolby Digital
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_Theater_System" title="Digital Theater System">
       DTS
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Surround_sound" title="Surround sound">
       surround sound
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
       <a href="#cite_note-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It also includes the original 1975 video of Bohemian Rhapsody.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 21 November 2005 it was once more re-released by Hollywood Records Catalogue Number 2061-62572-2 to celebrate the 30th anniversary of the album and its first single, "
      <a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">
       Bohemian Rhapsody
      </a>
      ". This release is accompanied by a DVD-Video disc with the same track listing featuring the original videos, old and new concert footage (including "'39" from the
      <a href="/wiki/Queen_%2B_Paul_Rodgers" title="Queen + Paul Rodgers">
       Queen + Paul Rodgers
      </a>
      tour and
      <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">
       Brian May
      </a>
      on the roof of
      <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">
       Buckingham Palace
      </a>
      playing "God Save the Queen") and audio commentary by all four bandmembers. It was on this commentary (and on
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_the_Studio_with_Redbeard" title="In the Studio with Redbeard">
        In the Studio with Redbeard
       </a>
      </i>
      , which devoted an episode to
      <i>
       A Night at the Opera
      </i>
      ) that May stated that had the album not been a success, Queen certainly would have disbanded.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 8 November 2010, record company
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_Music" title="Universal Music">
       Universal Music
      </a>
      announced a remastered and expanded reissue of the album set for release in May 2011. This as part of a new record deal between Queen and Universal Music, which meant Queen's association with
      <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">
       EMI
      </a>
      would come to an end after almost 40 years. According to Universal Music, all Queen albums were to be remastered and reissued in 2011. By September 2012 the reissue program will actually be complete.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Along with this came a 5.1 channel release of ANatO on Blu-Ray Audio
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listing">
       Track listing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Track listing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="tracklist" style="border-spacing: 0px; border-collapse: collapse; padding:4px">
      <tr>
       <th class="tlheader mbox-text" colspan="10" style="text-align: left; background-color: #fff">
        Side one
       </th>
       <td class="mbox-empty-cell">
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <th class="tlheader" scope="col" style="width: 2em; padding-left: 10px; padding-right: 10px; text-align: right; background-color: #eee">

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">
       Personnel
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Personnel">

       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Queen
      </dt>
     </dl>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">
        Freddie Mercury
       </a>
       
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lead_vocals" title="Lead vocals">
        lead
       </a>
       (except where noted below plus "God Save The Queen") and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Backing_vocals" title="Backing vocals">
        backing vocals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">
        piano
       </a>
       (credited as "Bechstein Debauchery" in liner notes),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-1">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         1
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Tack_piano" title="Tack piano">
        jangle piano
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodwind" title="Woodwind">
        woodwind
       </a>
       vocalizations on "Seaside Rendezvous"
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">
        Brian May
       </a>
       
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guitars" title="Guitars">
        guitars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukulele" title="Ukulele">
        ukulele
       </a>
       on "Good Company", backing vocals, lead vocals on "'39" and "Good Company",
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koto_(musical_instrument)" title="Koto (musical instrument)">
        toy koto
       </a>
       on "The Prophet's Song",
       <a href="/wiki/Harp" title="Harp">
        harp
       </a>
       on "Love of My Life", orchestral backdrops
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-1">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         1
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">
        Roger Taylor
       </a>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">
        drums
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Percussion_instrument" title="Percussion instrument">
        percussion
       </a>
       , lead vocals on "I'm in Love with My Car",
       <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">
        brass
       </a>
       vocalizations on "Seaside Rendezvous", backing vocals (Taylor is erroneously credited with merely percussion in the liner notes, when in truth he plays both drums and percussion)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-1">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         1
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
